			<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Braille</h1>
									<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">
									<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
								<div id="contentSub"></div>
												<div id="jump-to-nav" class="mw-jump">
					Jump to:					<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#mw-head">navigation</a>, 					<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#p-search">search</a>
				</div>
				<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div role="note" class="hatnote">This article is about the writing system used by people who are blind and have low vision. For other uses, see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Braille (disambiguation)">Braille (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<div style="font-size: xx-small; line-height: 1.6em; margin-left: 60px;">This audio file was created from a revision of the "<span class="fn">Braille</span>" article dated 2006-09-06, and does not reflect subsequent edits to the article. <div style="text-align: center; clear: both"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Spoken_articles" title="Wikipedia:Spoken articles">More spoken articles</a></b></div>
</div>
<p><b>Braille</b> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="// primary stress follows"></span><span title="&#39;b&#39; in &#39;buy&#39;">b</span><span title="&#39;r&#39; in &#39;rye&#39;">r</span><span title="/e/ long &#39;a&#39; in &#39;base&#39;">e</span><span title="&#39;l&#39; in &#39;lie&#39;">l</span></span>/</a></span></span> (<small>French pronunciation:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[baj]</a></span>) is a tactile <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Writing_system" title="Writing system">writing system</a> used by people who are <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blindness" class="mw-redirect" title="Blindness">blind</a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Visually_impaired" class="mw-redirect" title="Visually impaired">visually impaired</a>. It is traditionally written with embossed paper. Braille-users can read computer screens and other electronic supports thanks to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refreshable_braille_display" title="Refreshable braille display">refreshable braille displays</a>. They can write braille with the original <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slate_and_stylus" title="Slate and stylus">slate and stylus</a> or type it on a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_writer" class="mw-redirect" title="Braille writer">braille writer</a>, such as a portable <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_note-taker" class="mw-redirect" title="Braille note-taker">braille note-taker</a>, or on a computer that prints with a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_embosser" title="Braille embosser">braille embosser</a>.</p>
<p>Braille is named after its creator, Frenchman <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Braille" title="Louis Braille">Louis Braille</a>, who lost his eyesight due to a childhood accident. In 1824, at the age of 15, Braille developed his code for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="French alphabet">French alphabet</a> as an improvement on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Night_writing" title="Night writing">night writing</a>. He published his system, which subsequently included <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_notation" title="Musical notation">musical notation</a>, in 1829.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The second revision, published in 1837, was the first <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_numeral_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Binary numeral system">binary</a> form of writing developed in the modern era.</p>
<p>Braille characters are small rectangular blocks called <i>cells</i> that contain tiny palpable bumps called <i>raised dots</i>. The number and arrangement of these dots distinguish one character from another. Since the various braille alphabets originated as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Transcription_(linguistics)" title="Transcription (linguistics)">transcription</a> codes of printed writing systems, the mappings (sets of character designations) vary from language to language. Furthermore, in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Braille" title="English Braille">English Braille</a> there are three levels of encoding: Grade 1  a letter-by-letter transcription used for basic literacy; Grade 2  an addition of abbreviations and contractions; and Grade 3  various non-standardized personal <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shorthand" title="Shorthand">shorthands</a>.</p>
<p>Braille cells are not the only thing to appear in braille text. There may be embossed illustrations and graphs, with the lines either solid or made of series of dots, arrows, bullets that are larger than braille dots, etc. A full Braille cell includes six raised dots arranged in two lateral rows each having three dots.<sup id="cite_ref-Raised_Dots_3-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Raised_Dots-3">[3]</a></sup> The dot positions are identified by numbers from one through six.<sup id="cite_ref-Raised_Dots_3-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Raised_Dots-3">[3]</a></sup> 64 solutions are possible from using one or more dots.<sup id="cite_ref-Raised_Dots_3-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Raised_Dots-3">[3]</a></sup> A single cell can be used to represent an alphabet letter, number, punctuation mark, or even an entire word.<sup id="cite_ref-Raised_Dots_3-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Raised_Dots-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the face of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Screen_reader" title="Screen reader">screen-reader</a> software, braille usage has declined. However, braille education remains important for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Learning_to_read" title="Learning to read">developing reading skills</a> among blind and visually impaired children, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_literacy" title="Braille literacy">braille literacy</a> correlates with higher employment rates.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:DSC_4050-MR-Braille.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-DSC_4050-MR-Braille.jpg" width="220" height="296" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/DSC_4050-MR-Braille.jpg/330px-DSC_4050-MR-Braille.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/54/DSC_4050-MR-Braille.jpg 2x" data-file-width="363" data-file-height="489"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:DSC_4050-MR-Braille.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Braille code where the word <span lang="fr-Brai"><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1234) U+280F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1235) U+2817" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-15) U+2811" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-134) U+280D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-24) U+280A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-15) U+2811" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1235) U+2817" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span></span> (<span lang="fr"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/premier#French" class="extiw" title="wikt:premier">premier</a></span>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> for first) can be read.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braille was based on a tactile military <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code" title="Code">code</a> called <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Night_writing" title="Night writing">night writing</a>, developed by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charles_Barbier" title="Charles Barbier">Charles Barbier</a> in response to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>'s demand for a means for soldiers to communicate silently at night and without a light source.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> In Barbier's system, sets of 12 embossed dots encoded 36 different sounds. It proved to be too difficult for soldiers to recognize by touch, and was rejected by the military. In 1821 Barbier visited the Royal Institute for the Blind in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>, where he met Louis Braille. Braille identified two major defects of the code: first, by representing only sounds, the code was unable to render the orthography of the words; second, the human finger could not encompass the whole 12-dot symbol without moving, and so could not move rapidly from one symbol to another. Braille's solution was to use 6-dot cells and to assign a specific pattern to each letter of the alphabet.<sup id="cite_ref-No.C3.ABlle_Roy_5-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-No.C3.ABlle_Roy-5">[5]</a></sup> At first, braille was a one-to-one transliteration of French orthography, but soon various abbreviations, contractions, and even <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logogram" title="Logogram">logograms</a> were developed, creating a system much more like shorthand.<sup id="cite_ref-digital_6-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-digital-6">[6]</a></sup> The expanded English system, called <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Grade-2_Braille" class="mw-redirect" title="Grade-2 Braille">Grade-2 Braille</a>, was complete by 1905. To the blind, Braille is an independent writing system, rather than a code of printed orthography.<sup id="cite_ref-D.26B_7-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-D.26B-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Derivation">Derivation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Derivation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Braille is derived from the Latin alphabet, albeit indirectly. In Braille's original system, the dot patterns were assigned to letters according to their position within the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Collating_sequence" class="mw-redirect" title="Collating sequence">alphabetic order</a> of the French alphabet, with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">accented</a> letters and <i>w</i> sorted at the end.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>The first ten letters of the alphabet, <i>aj,</i> use the upper four dot positions: <span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12) U+2803" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-14) U+2809" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-145) U+2819" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-15) U+2811" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-124) U+280B" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1245) U+281B" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-125) U+2813" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-24) U+280A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-245) U+281A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (black dots in the table below). These stand for the ten digits <i>19</i> and <i>0</i> in a system parallel to Hebrew <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gematria" title="Gematria">gematria</a> and Greek <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Isopsephy" title="Isopsephy">isopsephy</a>. (Though the dots are assigned in no obvious order, the cells with the fewest dots are assigned to the first three letters (and lowest digits), <i>abc = 123</i> (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12) U+2803" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-14) U+2809" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>), and to the three vowels in this part of the alphabet, <i>aei</i> (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-15) U+2811" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-24) U+280A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>), whereas the even digits, <i>4, 6, 8, 0</i> (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-145) U+2819" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-124) U+280B" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-125) U+2813" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-245) U+281A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>), are corners/right angles.)</p>
<p>The next ten letters, <i>kt,</i> are identical to <i>aj,</i> respectively, apart from the addition of a dot at position 3 (red dots in the table): <span title="  (braille pattern dots-13) U+2805" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-123) U+2807" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-134) U+280D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1345) U+281D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-135) U+2815" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1234) U+280F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12345) U+281F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1235) U+2817" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-234) U+280E" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-2345) U+281E" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>:</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>Derivation (colored dots) of the 26 letters of the alphabet from the 10 numeric digits (black dots)</caption>
<tbody><tr align="center">
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_A1.svg" class="image"><img alt="Braille A1.svg" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_A1.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Braille_A1.svg/60px-Braille_A1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Braille_A1.svg/80px-Braille_A1.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_B2.svg" class="image"><img alt="Braille B2.svg" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_B2.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Braille_B2.svg/60px-Braille_B2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Braille_B2.svg/80px-Braille_B2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_C3.svg" class="image"><img alt="Braille C3.svg" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_C3.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Braille_C3.svg/60px-Braille_C3.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ca/Braille_C3.svg/80px-Braille_C3.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>

<p>The next ten letters (the next "<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/decade#English" class="extiw" title="wikt:decade">decade</a>") are the same again, but with dots also at positions both 3 and 6 (green dots). Here <i>w</i> was left out as not being a part of the official French alphabet at the time of Braille's life; the French braille order is <i>u v x y z     </i> (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-136) U+2825" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1236) U+2827" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1346) U+282D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-13456) U+283D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1356) U+2835" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12346) U+282F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-123456) U+283F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12356) U+2837" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-2346) U+282E" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-23456) U+283E" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<p>The next ten, ending in <i>w</i>, are the same again, except that for this series position 6 (purple dot) is used without position 3. These are <i>         w</i> (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-16) U+2821" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-126) U+2823" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-146) U+2829" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1456) U+2839" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-156) U+2831" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1246) U+282B" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12456) U+283B" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1256) U+2833" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-246) U+282A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-2456) U+283A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>).<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>aj</i> series lowered by one dot space (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-2) U+2802" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-23) U+2806" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-25) U+2812" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-256) U+2832" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-26) U+2822" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-235) U+2816" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-2356) U+2836" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-236) U+2826" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-35) U+2814" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-356) U+2834" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>) are used for punctuation. Letters <i>a</i> <span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> and <i>c</i> <span title="  (braille pattern dots-14) U+2809" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>, which only use dots in the top row, were lowered two places for the apostrophe and hyphen: <span title="  (braille pattern dots-3) U+2804" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-36) U+2824" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>. (These are the decade diacritics, at left in the table below, of the second and third decade.)</p>
<p>In addition, there are ten patterns that are based on the first two letters (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12) U+2803" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>) shifted to the right; these were assigned to non-French letters (<i>  </i> <span title="  (braille pattern dots-34) U+280C" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-345) U+281C" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-346) U+282C" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>), or serve non-letter functions: <span title="  (braille pattern dots-4) U+2808" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (superscript; in English the accent mark), <span title="  (braille pattern dots-45) U+2818" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (currency prefix), <span title="  (braille pattern dots-46) U+2828" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (capital, in English the decimal point), <span title="  (braille pattern dots-3456) U+283C" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (number sign), <span title="  (braille pattern dots-456) U+2838" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (emphasis mark), <span title="  (braille pattern dots-5) U+2810" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> (symbol prefix).</p>
<dl>
<dd>
<table class="wikitable">
<caption>The 64 braille cells<span id="upper-half_cells"></span><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-11">[a]</a></sup></caption>

</tbody></table>
</dd>
</dl>
<p>Originally there had been nine decades. The fifth through ninth used dashes as well as dots, but proved to be impractical and were soon abandoned. These could be replaced with what we now know as the number sign (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-3456) U+283C" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>), though that only caught on for the digits (old 5th decade  modern 1st decade). The dash occupying the top row of the original sixth decade was simply dropped, producing the modern fifth decade. (See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1829_braille" title="1829 braille">1829 braille</a>.)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Assignment">Assignment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Assignment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Historically, there have been three principles in assigning the values of a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_writing" class="mw-redirect" title="Linear writing">linear script</a> (print) to braille: Using Louis Braille's original French letter values; reassigning the braille letters according to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sort_order" class="mw-redirect" title="Sort order">sort order</a> of the print alphabet being transcribed; and reassigning the letters to improve the efficiency of writing in braille.</p>
<p>Under international consensus, most braille alphabets follow the French sorting order for the 26 letters of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ISO_basic_Latin_alphabet" title="ISO basic Latin alphabet">basic Latin alphabet</a>, and there have been attempts at unifying the letters beyond these 26 (see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_braille" class="mw-redirect" title="International braille">international braille</a>), though differences remain, for example in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/German_Braille" title="German Braille">German Braille</a> and the contractions of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Braille" title="English Braille">English Braille</a>. This unification avoids the chaos of each nation reordering the braille code to match the sorting order of its print alphabet, as happened in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Algerian_Braille" title="Algerian Braille">Algerian Braille</a>, where braille codes were numerically reassigned to match the order of the Arabic alphabet and bear little relation to the values used in other countries (compare modern <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arabic_Braille" title="Arabic Braille">Arabic Braille</a>, which uses the French sorting order), and as happened in an early American version of English Braille, where the letters <i>w, x, y, z</i> were reassigned to match English alphabetical order. A convention sometimes seen for letters beyond the basic 26 is to exploit the physical symmetry of braille patterns iconically, for example, by assigning a reversed <i>n</i> to <i></i> or an inverted <i>s</i> to <i>sh</i>. (See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hungarian_Braille" title="Hungarian Braille">Hungarian Braille</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bharati_Braille" title="Bharati Braille">Bharati Braille</a>, which do this to some extent.)</p>
<p>A third principle was to assign braille codes according to frequency, with the simplest patterns (quickest ones to write) assigned to the most frequent letters of the alphabet. Such frequency-based alphabets were used in Germany and the United States in the 19th century (see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Braille" title="American Braille">American Braille</a>), but none are attested in modern use. Finally, there are braille scripts which don't order the codes numerically at all, such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Japanese_Braille" title="Japanese Braille">Japanese Braille</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Korean_Braille" title="Korean Braille">Korean Braille</a>, which are based on more abstract principles of syllable composition.</p>
<p>Academic texts are sometimes written in a script of eight dots per cell rather than six, enabling them to encode a greater number of symbols. (See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Gardner%E2%80%93Salinas_braille_codes" title="GardnerSalinas braille codes">GardnerSalinas braille codes</a>.) <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Luxembourgish_Braille" title="Luxembourgish Braille">Luxembourgish Braille</a> has adopted eight-dot cells for general use; for example, it adds a dot below each letter to derive its capital variant.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Form">Form</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Form">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alianca_braille.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Alianca_braille.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alianca_braille.JPG/330px-Alianca_braille.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Alianca_braille.JPG/440px-Alianca_braille.JPG 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="960"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Alianca_braille.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Silver wedding bands with names <i>Henri(que)</i> and <i>Tita</i> written in braille</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braille was the first writing system with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_numeral_system" class="mw-redirect" title="Binary numeral system">binary</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_encoding" title="Character encoding">encoding</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-digital_6-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-digital-6">[6]</a></sup> The system as devised by Braille consists of two parts:<sup id="cite_ref-D.26B_7-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-D.26B-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<ol>
<li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Character_encoding" title="Character encoding">Character encoding</a> that mapped characters of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_alphabet" class="mw-redirect" title="French alphabet">French alphabet</a> to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tuple" title="Tuple">tuples</a> of six <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bit" title="Bit">bits</a> (the dots),</li>
<li>The physical representation of those six-bit characters with raised dots in a braille cell.</li>
</ol>
<p>Within an individual cell, the dot positions are arranged as two columns of three positions. A raised dot can appear in any of the six positions, producing sixty-four (2<sup>6</sup>) possible patterns, including one in which there are no raised dots. For reference purposes, a pattern is commonly described by listing the positions where dots are raised, the positions being universally numbered, from top to bottom, as 1 to 3 on the left and 4 to 6 on the right. For example, dot pattern 1-3-4 describe a cell with three dots raised, at the top and bottom in the left column and at the top of the right column: that is, the letter <span title="  (braille pattern dots-134) U+280D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>m</i>. The lines of horizontal braille text are separated by a space, much like visible printed text, so that the dots of one line can be differentiated from the braille text above and below. Different assignments of braille codes (or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Code_page" title="Code page">code pages</a>) are used to map the character sets of different printed scripts to the six-bit cells. Braille assignments have also been created for mathematical and musical notation. However, because the six-dot braille cell allows only 64 (2<sup>6</sup>) patterns, including the space, the characters of a braille script commonly have multiple values, depending on their context. That is, character mapping between print and braille is not one-to-one. For example, the character <span title="  (braille pattern dots-145) U+2819" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> corresponds in print to both the letter <i>d</i> and the digit <i>4</i>.</p>
<p>In addition to simple encoding, many braille alphabets use contractions to reduce the size of braille texts and to increase reading speed. (See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Braille#Contractions" title="English Braille">Contracted braille</a>)</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Writing_braille">Writing braille</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Writing braille">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_Writer.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Braille_Writer.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Braille_Writer.jpg/330px-Braille_Writer.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Braille_Writer.jpg/440px-Braille_Writer.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_Writer.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Braille typewriter</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Braille may be produced by hand using a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Slate_and_stylus" title="Slate and stylus">slate and stylus</a> in which each dot is created from the back of the page, writing in mirror image, or it may be produced on a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_typewriter" class="mw-redirect" title="Braille typewriter">braille typewriter</a> or <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Perkins_Brailler" title="Perkins Brailler">Perkins Brailler</a>, or an electronic Brailler or eBrailler. Because braille letters cannot be effectively erased and written over if an error is made, an error is overwritten with all six dots (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-123456) U+283F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>). <i>Interpoint</i> refers to braille printing that is offset, so that the paper can be embossed on both sides, with the dots on one side appearing between the divots that form the dots on the other (see the photo in the box at the top of this article for an example). Using a computer or other electronic device, braille may be produced with a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_embosser" title="Braille embosser">braille embosser</a> (printer) or a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refreshable_braille_display" title="Refreshable braille display">refreshable braille display</a> (screen).</p>
<p><span id="Eight-dot_braille"></span>Braille has been extended to an 8-dot code, particularly for use with braille embossers and refreshable braille displays. In 8-dot braille the additional dots are added at the bottom of the cell, giving a matrix 4 dots high by 2 dots wide. The additional dots are given the numbers 7 (for the lower-left dot) and 8 (for the lower-right dot). Eight-dot braille has the advantages that the case of an individual letter is directly coded in the cell containing the letter and that all the printable <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/ASCII" title="ASCII">ASCII</a> characters can be represented in a single cell. All 256 (2<sup>8</sup>) possible combinations of 8 dots are encoded by the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> standard. Braille with six dots is frequently stored as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_ASCII" title="Braille ASCII">Braille ASCII</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Letters">Letters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Letters">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The first 25 braille letters, up through the first half of the 3rd decade, transcribe <i>az</i> (skipping <i>w</i>). In English Braille, the rest of that decade is rounded out with the ligatures <i>and, for, of, the,</i> and <i>with</i>. Omitting dot 3 from these forms the 4th decade, the ligatures <i>ch, gh, sh, th, wh, ed, er, ou, ow</i> and the letter <i>w</i>.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr align="center">
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_%C3%85.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-16) U+2821"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-16) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Braille_%C3%85.svg/60px-Braille_%C3%85.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/Braille_%C3%85.svg/80px-Braille_%C3%85.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>

<p>(See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Braille" title="English Braille">English Braille</a>.)</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Formatting">Formatting</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Formatting">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Various formatting marks affect the values of the letters that follow them. They have no direct equivalent in print. The most important in English Braille are:</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr align="center">
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_CapitalSign.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-6) U+2820"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-6) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_CapitalSign.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Braille_CapitalSign.svg/60px-Braille_CapitalSign.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Braille_CapitalSign.svg/80px-Braille_CapitalSign.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_NumberSign.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-3456) U+283C"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-3456) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_NumberSign.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Braille_NumberSign.svg/60px-Braille_NumberSign.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Braille_NumberSign.svg/80px-Braille_NumberSign.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
</tr>
<tr align="center">
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Capital_letter" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital letter">Capital</a><br>
follows</td>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Number" title="Number">Number</a><br>
follows</td>
</tr>
</tbody></table>
<p>That is, <span title="  (braille pattern dots-6) U+2820" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> is read as capital 'A', and <span title="  (braille pattern dots-3456) U+283C" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> as the digit '1'.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Punctuation">Punctuation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Punctuation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><span title="  (braille pattern dots-236) U+2826" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> is both the question mark and the opening quotation mark. Its reading depends on whether it occurs before a word or after.</p>
<p><span title="  (braille pattern dots-2356) U+2836" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> is used for both opening and closing parentheses. Its placement relative to spaces and other characters determines its interpretation.</p>
<p>Punctuation varies from language to language. For example, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Braille" title="French Braille">French Braille</a> uses <span title="  (braille pattern dots-26) U+2822" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> for its question mark and swaps the quotation marks and parentheses (to <span title="  (braille pattern dots-2356) U+2836" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> and <span title="  (braille pattern dots-236) U+2826" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-356) U+2834" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>); it uses the period (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-256) U+2832" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>) for the decimal point, as in print, and the decimal point (<span title="  (braille pattern dots-46) U+2828" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>) to mark capitalization.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contractions">Contractions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Contractions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">For a full list of abbreviations and contractions in English, see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/English_Braille#Contractions" title="English Braille">English Braille &nbsp;Contractions</a>.</div>
<p>Braille contractions are words and affixes that are shortened so that they take up fewer cells. In English Braille, for example, the word <i>afternoon</i> is written with just three letters, <span title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-124) U+280B" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1345) U+281D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> afn, much like <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Stenoscript" title="Stenoscript">stenoscript</a>. There are also several abbreviation marks that create what are effectively <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Logogram" title="Logogram">logograms</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-D.26B_7-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-D.26B-7">[7]</a></sup> The most common of these is dot 5, which combines with the first letter of words. With the letter <span title="  (braille pattern dots-134) U+280D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>m</i>, the resulting word is <span title="  (braille pattern dots-5) U+2810" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-134) U+280D" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>mother</i>. There are also <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ligature_(typography)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ligature (typography)">ligatures</a> ("contracted" letters), which are single letters in braille but correspond to more than one letter in print. The letter <span title="  (braille pattern dots-12346) U+282F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>and</i>, for example, is used to write words with the sequence <i>a-n-d</i> in them, such as <span title="  (braille pattern dots-125) U+2813" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-12346) U+282F" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>hand</i>.</p>
<table class="wikitable">
<tbody><tr>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_A1.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-1) U+2801"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-1) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_A1.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Braille_A1.svg/60px-Braille_A1.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Braille_A1.svg/80px-Braille_A1.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_F6.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-124) U+280B"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-124) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_F6.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Braille_F6.svg/60px-Braille_F6.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Braille_F6.svg/80px-Braille_F6.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_N.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-1345) U+281D"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-1345) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_N.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Braille_N.svg/60px-Braille_N.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Braille_N.svg/80px-Braille_N.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_ContractionPrefix.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-5) U+2810"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-5) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_ContractionPrefix.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Braille_ContractionPrefix.svg/60px-Braille_ContractionPrefix.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Braille_ContractionPrefix.svg/80px-Braille_ContractionPrefix.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_M.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-134) U+280D"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-134) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_M.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Braille_M.svg/60px-Braille_M.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9b/Braille_M.svg/80px-Braille_M.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
<td><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_H8.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-125) U+2813"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-125) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_H8.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Braille_H8.svg/60px-Braille_H8.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Braille_H8.svg/80px-Braille_H8.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_AND.svg" class="image" title="  (braille pattern dots-12346) U+282F"><img alt=" (braille pattern dots-12346) " src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/40px-Braille_AND.svg.png" width="40" height="56" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Braille_AND.svg/60px-Braille_AND.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Braille_AND.svg/80px-Braille_AND.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="154" data-file-height="215"></a></td>
