<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Page_dimensions">Page dimensions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Page dimensions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Most <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_embosser" title="Braille embosser">braille embossers</a> support between 34 and 40 cells per line, and 25 lines per page.</p>
<p>A manually operated Perkins braille typewriter supports a maximum of 42 cells per line (its margins are adjustable), and typical paper allows 25 lines per page.</p>
<p>A large interlining Stainsby has 36 cells per line and 18 lines per page.</p>
<p>An A4-sized Marburg braille frame, which allows interpoint braille (dots on both sides of the page, offset so they do not interfere with each other) has 30 cells per line and 27 lines per page.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Literacy">Literacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Literacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_literacy" title="Braille literacy">Braille literacy</a></div>
<p>A sighted child who is reading at a basic level should be able to understand common words and answer simple questions about the information presented.<sup id="cite_ref-Grover_12-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Grover-12">[11]</a></sup> The child should also have enough fluency to get through the material in a timely manner. Over the course of a child's education, these foundations are built upon to teach higher levels of math, science, and comprehension skills.<sup id="cite_ref-Grover_12-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Grover-12">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>Children who are blind not only have the education disadvantage of not being able to see  they also miss out on fundamental parts of early and advanced education if not provided with the necessary tools. Children who are blind or visually impaired can begin learning pre-braille skills from a very young age to become fluent braille readers as they get older.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._braille_literacy_statistics">U.S. braille literacy statistics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: U.S. braille literacy statistics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1960, 50% of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Legally_blind" class="mw-redirect" title="Legally blind">legally blind</a>, school-age children were able to read braille in the U.S.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ranalli2008_14-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ranalli2008-14">[13]</a></sup> According to the 2015 <i>Annual Report</i> from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Printing_House_for_the_Blind" title="American Printing House for the Blind">American Printing House for the Blind</a>, there were 61,739 legally blind students registered in the U.S. Of these, 8.6% (5,333) were registered as braille readers, 31% (19,109) as visual readers, 9.4% (5,795) as auditory readers, 17% (10,470) as pre-readers, and 34% (21,032) as non-readers.<sup id="cite_ref-Blind2013_15-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Blind2013-15">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>There are numerous causes for the decline in braille usage, including school budget constraints, technology advancement, and different philosophical views over how <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Blindness" class="mw-redirect" title="Blindness">blind</a> children should be educated.<sup id="cite_ref-Ruby_Riles_16-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ruby_Riles-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>A key turning point for braille literacy was the passage of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rehabilitation_Act_of_1973" title="Rehabilitation Act of 1973">Rehabilitation Act of 1973</a>, an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Act_of_Congress" title="Act of Congress">act of Congress</a> that moved thousands of children from specialized schools for the blind into <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainstreaming_(education)" title="Mainstreaming (education)">mainstream</a> public schools.<sup id="cite_ref-Ranalli2008_14-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ranalli2008-14">[13]</a></sup> Because only a small percentage of public schools could afford to train and hire braille-qualified teachers, braille literacy has declined since the law took effect.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ranalli2008_14-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ranalli2008-14">[13]</a></sup> Braille literacy rates have improved slightly since the bill was passed,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (November 2011)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> in part because of pressure from consumers and advocacy groups that has led 27 states to pass legislation mandating that children who are legally blind be given the opportunity to learn braille.<sup id="cite_ref-Ruby_Riles_16-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ruby_Riles-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1998 there were 57,425 legally blind students registered in the United States, but only 10% (5,461) of them used braille as their primary reading medium.<sup id="cite_ref-Blind1999_17-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Blind1999-17">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ebnet2001_18-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ebnet2001-18">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Early braille education is crucial to literacy for a blind or low-vision child. A study conducted in the state of Washington found that people who learned braille at an early age did just as well, if not better, than their sighted peers in several areas, including vocabulary and comprehension. In the preliminary adult study, while evaluating the correlation between adult literacy skills and employment, it was found that 44% of the participants who had learned to read in braille were unemployed, compared to the 77% unemployment rate of those who had learned to read using print.<sup id="cite_ref-Ph2004_19-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ph2004-19">[18]</a></sup> Currently, among the estimated 85,000 blind adults in the United States, 90% of those who are braille-literate are employed. Among adults who do not know braille, only 33% are employed.<sup id="cite_ref-Ranalli2008_14-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ranalli2008-14">[13]</a></sup> Statistically, history has proven that braille reading proficiency provides an essential skill set that allows blind or low-vision children to compete with their sighted peers in a school environment and later in life as they enter the workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-Ruby_Riles_16-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-Ruby_Riles-16">[15]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">United Kingdom</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Though braille is thought to be the main way blind people read and write, in Britain (for example) out of the reported 2 million blind and low vision population, it is estimated that only around 1520 thousand people use braille.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-20">[19]</a></sup> Younger people are turning to electronic text on computers with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Screen_reader" title="Screen reader">screen reader</a> software instead, a more portable communication method that they can use with their friends. A debate has started on how to make braille more attractive and for more teachers to be available to teach it.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Braille_transcription">Braille transcription</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Braille transcription">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><span id="keyboard"></span></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG/330px-Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ee/Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG/440px-Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_on_tablet_box.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Braille on a box of tablets. The raised Braille reads 'plavix'.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_book.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Braille_book.JPG" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Braille_book.JPG/330px-Braille_book.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fa/Braille_book.JPG/440px-Braille_book.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2575" data-file-height="1788"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_book.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Braille book and the same book in standard inkprint</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Although it is possible to transcribe print by simply substituting the equivalent braille character for its printed equivalent, in English such a character-by-character transcription (known as <i>uncontracted braille</i>) is only used by beginners.</p>
<p>Braille characters are much larger than their printed equivalents, and the standard 11" by 11.5" (28&nbsp;cm  30&nbsp;cm) page has room for only 25 lines of 43 characters. To reduce space and increase reading speed, most braille alphabets and orthographies use ligatures, abbreviations, and contractions. Virtually all English Braille books are transcribed in this <i>contracted braille,</i> which adds an additional layer of complexity to English orthography: The Library of Congress's <i>Instruction Manual for Braille Transcribing</i><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> runs to over 300 pages and braille transcribers must pass certification tests.</p>
<p>Fully contracted braille is known as <i>Grade 2 Braille</i>. There is an intermediate form between Computer Brailleone-for-one identity with printand Grade 2, which is called Grade 1 Braille. In Grade 1 the capital-sign and Number sign are used, and most punctuation marks are shown using their Grade 2 values.</p>
<p>The system of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Contraction_(grammar)" title="Contraction (grammar)">contractions</a> in English Braille begins with a set of 23 words which are contracted to single characters. Thus the word <i>but</i> is contracted to the single letter <i>b,</i> <i>can</i> to <i>c</i>, <i>do</i> to <i>d</i>, and so on. Even this simple rule creates issues requiring special cases; for example, <i>d</i> is, specifically, an abbreviation of the verb <i>do;</i> the noun <i>do</i> representing the note of the musical scale is a different word, and must be spelled out.</p>
<p>Portions of words may be contracted, and many rules govern this process. For example, the character with dots 2-3-5 (the letter "f" lowered in the braille cell) stands for "ff" when used in the middle of a word. At the beginning of a word, this same character stands for the word "to"; the character is written in braille with no space following it. (This contraction was removed in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_English_Braille_Code" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified English Braille Code">Unified English Braille Code</a>.) At the end of a word, the same character represents an exclamation point.</p>
<p>Some contractions are more similar than their print equivalents. For example, the contraction lr, meaning 'letter', differs from ll, meaning 'little', only in adding one dot to the second l: <span title="  (braille pattern dots-123) U+2807" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-123) U+2807" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>little</i>, <span title="  (braille pattern dots-123) U+2807" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span><span title="  (braille pattern dots-1235) U+2817" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span> <i>letter</i>. This causes greater confusion between the braille spellings of these words and can hinder the learning process of contracted braille.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>The contraction rules take into account the linguistic structure of the word; thus, contractions are generally not to be used when their use would alter the usual braille form of a base word to which a prefix or suffix has been added. Some portions of the transcription rules are not fully codified and rely on the judgment of the transcriber. Thus, when the contraction rules permit the same word in more than one way, preference is given to "the contraction that more nearly approximates correct pronunciation."</p>
<p><i>Grade 3 Braille</i><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup> is a variety of non-standardized systems that include many additional shorthand-like contraction. They are not used for publication, but by individuals for their personal convenience.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Braille_translation_software">Braille translation software</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Braille translation software">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When people produce braille, this is called braille transcription. When computer software produces braille, this is called braille translation. Braille translation software exists to handle most of the common languages of the world, and many technical areas, such as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mathematical_notation" title="Mathematical notation">mathematical notation</a>), for example <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WIMATS" title="WIMATS">WIMATS</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a> (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Musical_notation" title="Musical notation">musical notation</a>), and tactile graphics.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Braille-reading_techniques">Braille-reading techniques</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Braille-reading techniques">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since braille is one of the few writing systems where tactile perception is used, as opposed to visual perception, a braille reader must develop new skills. One skill important for braille readers is the ability to create smooth and even pressures when running one's fingers along the words. There are many different styles and techniques used for the understanding and development of braille, even though a study by B. F. Holland<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> suggests that there is no specific technique that is superior to any other.</p>
<p>Another study by Lowenfield &amp; Abel<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup> shows that braille could be read "the fastest and best... by students who read using the index fingers of both hands." Another important reading skill emphasized in this study is to finish reading the end of a line with the right hand and to find the beginning of the next line with the left hand simultaneously. One final conclusion drawn by both Lowenfield and Abel is that children have difficulty using both hands independently where the right hand is the dominant hand. But this hand preference does not correlate to other activities.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="International_uniformity">International uniformity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: International uniformity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/International_uniformity_of_braille" class="mw-redirect" title="International uniformity of braille">International uniformity of braille</a></div>
<p><span id="Grade_1_braille"></span></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg/330px-Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg/440px-Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2014" data-file-height="1511"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Rapperswil_-_Duftrosengarten_20080222_005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Braille plate at <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Duftrosengarten" class="mw-redirect" title="Duftrosengarten">Duftrosengarten</a></i> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rapperswil" title="Rapperswil">Rapperswil</a>, Switzerland</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>When braille was first adapted to languages other than French, many schemes were adopted, including mapping the native alphabet to the alphabetical order of French  e.g. in English W, which was not in the French alphabet at the time, is mapped to braille X, X to Y, Y to Z, and Z to the first French accented letter  or completely rearranging the alphabet such that common letters are represented by the simplest braille patterns. Consequently, mutual intelligibility was greatly hindered by this state of affairs. In 1878, the International Congress on Work for the Blind, held in Paris, proposed an international braille standard, where braille codes for different languages and scripts would be based, not on the order of a particular alphabet, but on phonetic correspondence and transliteration to Latin.<sup id="cite_ref-IntlBraille_26-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-IntlBraille-26">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>This unified braille has been applied to the languages of India and Africa, Arabic, Vietnamese, Hebrew, Russian, and Armenian, as well as nearly all Latin-script languages. Greek, for example, <i>gamma</i> is written as Latin <i>g</i>, despite the fact that it has the alphabetic position of <i>c</i>; Hebrew <i>bet</i>, the second letter of the alphabet and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">cognate</a> with the Latin letter <i>b</i>, is sometimes pronounced /b/ and sometimes /v/, and is written <i>b</i> or <i>v</i> accordingly; Russian <i>ts</i> is written as <i>c</i>, which is the usual letter for /ts/ in those Slavic languages that use the Latin alphabet; and Arabic <i>f</i> is written as <i>f</i>, despite being historically <i>p</i>, and occurring in that part of the Arabic alphabet (between historic <i>o</i> and <i>q</i>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_braille_conventions">Other braille conventions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Other braille conventions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Other systems for assigning values to braille patterns are also followed, beside the simple mapping of the alphabetical order onto the original French order. Some braille alphabets start with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unified_braille" class="mw-redirect" title="Unified braille">unified braille</a>, and then diverge significantly based on the phonology of the target languages, while others diverge even further.</p>
<p>In the various Chinese systems, traditional braille values are used for initial consonants and the simple vowels. In both <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mainland_Chinese_Braille" title="Mainland Chinese Braille">Mandarin</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cantonese_braille" class="mw-redirect" title="Cantonese braille">Cantonese Braille</a>, however, characters have different readings depending on whether they are placed in syllable-initial (onset) or syllable-final (rime) position. For instance, the cell for Latin <i>k</i>, <span title="  (braille pattern dots-13) U+2805" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>, represents Cantonese <i>k</i> (<i>g</i> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yale_romanization_of_Cantonese" title="Yale romanization of Cantonese">Yale</a> and other modern romanizations) when initial, but <i>aak</i> when final, while Latin <i>j</i>, <span title="  (braille pattern dots-245) U+281A" style="background: #f4f4f4; font-size:100%; margin:1px 2px 0 0;"></span>, represents Cantonese initial <i>j</i> but final <i>oei</i>.</p>
<p>Novel systems of braille mapping include Korean, which adopts separate syllable-initial and syllable-final forms for its consonants, explicitly grouping braille cells into syllabic groups in the same way as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hangul" title="Hangul">hangul</a>. Japanese, meanwhile, combines independent vowel dot patterns and modifier consonant dot patterns into a single braille cell  an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Abugida" title="Abugida">abugida</a> representation of each Japanese <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mora_(linguistics)#Japanese" title="Mora (linguistics)">mora</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Uses">Uses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Uses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_wine_label.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Braille_wine_label.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Braille_wine_label.jpg/330px-Braille_wine_label.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/04/Braille_wine_label.jpg/440px-Braille_wine_label.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Braille_wine_label.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A bottle of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chapoutier" title="Chapoutier">Chapoutier</a> wine, with braille on the label</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bahnhofsplan_f%C3%BCr_Blinde,_Hannover_Hbf,_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="./Braille - Wikipedia_files/220px-Bahnhofsplan_fr_Blinde,_Hannover_Hbf,_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Bahnhofsplan_f%C3%BCr_Blinde%2C_Hannover_Hbf%2C_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg/330px-Bahnhofsplan_f%C3%BCr_Blinde%2C_Hannover_Hbf%2C_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/Bahnhofsplan_f%C3%BCr_Blinde%2C_Hannover_Hbf%2C_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg/440px-Bahnhofsplan_f%C3%BCr_Blinde%2C_Hannover_Hbf%2C_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2816" data-file-height="2112"></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Bahnhofsplan_f%C3%BCr_Blinde,_Hannover_Hbf,_Ausschnitt_Eingangsbereich.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An embossed map of a German train station, with braille text</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The current series of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Banknotes_of_the_Canadian_dollar" title="Banknotes of the Canadian dollar">Canadian banknotes</a> has a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canadian_currency_tactile_feature" title="Canadian currency tactile feature">tactile feature</a> consisting of raised dots that indicate the denomination, allowing bills to be easily identified by blind or low vision people. It does not use standard braille; rather, the feature uses a system developed in consultation with blind and low vision Canadians after research indicated that braille was not sufficiently robust and that not all potential users read braille. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mexican_peso#Series_D" title="Mexican peso">Mexican bank notes</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indian_rupee" title="Indian rupee">Indian rupee</a> notes, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Israeli_New_Shekel" class="mw-redirect" title="Israeli New Shekel">Israeli New Shekel</a> notes,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Russian_Ruble" class="mw-redirect" title="Russian Ruble">Russian Ruble</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Swiss_Franc" class="mw-redirect" title="Swiss Franc">Swiss Franc</a> notes also have special raised symbols to make them identifiable by persons who are blind or low vision.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/India" title="India">India</a> there are instances where the parliament acts have been published in braille, such as <i>The Right to Information Act</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the United States, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Americans_with_Disabilities_Act_of_1990" title="Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990">Americans with Disabilities Act of 1990</a><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> requires various building signage to be in braille.</p>
<p>In the United Kingdom, it is required that medicines have the name of the medicine in Braille on the labelling.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup></p>
<p>Australia also recently introduced the tactile feature onto their five dollar banknote<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Unicode">Unicode</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Unicode">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicode_braille_patterns" class="mw-redirect" title="Unicode braille patterns">Unicode braille patterns</a></div>
<p>Braille was added to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Unicode" title="Unicode">Unicode</a> Standard in September, 1999 with the release of version 3.0.</p>
<p>Most <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_embosser" title="Braille embosser">braille embossers</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Refreshable_braille_display" title="Refreshable braille display">refreshable braille displays</a> do not support Unicode, using instead 6-dot <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille_ASCII" title="Braille ASCII">braille ASCII</a>. Some embossers have proprietary control codes for 8-dot braille or for full graphics mode, where dots may be placed anywhere on the page without leaving any space between braille cells, so that continuous lines can be drawn in diagrams, but these are rarely used and are not standard.</p>
<p>The Unicode standard encodes 8-dot braille glyphs according to their binary appearance, rather than following their assigned numeric order. Dot 1 corresponds to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Least_significant_bit" title="Least significant bit">least significant bit</a> of the low byte of the Unicode scalar value, and dot 8 to the high bit of that byte.</p>
<p>The Unicode block for braille is U+2800 ... U+28FF:</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Observation">Observation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Observation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Every year on 4 January, World Braille Day is observed internationally to commemorate the birth of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Louis_Braille" title="Louis Braille">Louis Braille</a> and to recognize his efforts. However, the event is not considered a public holiday.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Braille&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">
<ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-11"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_ref-11"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up </span>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The characters have been arranged by decade, with decade diacritics listed at left, and supplementary characters included on the right according to their diacritic. See <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1829_braille" title="1829 braille">1829 braille</a>, where the 12 characters listed in the first line are used for shorthand and are found in this order for the 12 notes of plainsong notation, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/French_Braille" title="French Braille">French Braille</a>, where the 'final' form of Braille's alphabet is laid out in the same way. However, modern tables often organize the supplementary characters differently: Those with a dot 3 are listed as a 6th group of 6 characters, and those with dots only on the right side are listed as a 7th group of 7, without anything in common with the columns the characters are listed under.</span></li>
</ol>
</div>

<li id="cite_note-9"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_ref-9"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up </span>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The values of the letters after <i>z</i> differ from language to language; these are Braille's assignments for French.</span></li>
<li id="cite_note-10"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Braille?oldformat=true#cite_ref-10"><span class="cite-accessibility-label">Jump up </span>^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><i>W</i> had been tacked onto the 39 letters of the French alphabet to accommodate English.</span></li>
